  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2212330719?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062104892" href="/book/show/16248113-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=that-setting-tho">that-setting-tho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fairytale">fairytale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=from-publisher-author">from-publisher-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2212330719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5732139895144374740">AFGHASDFGASHDF THIS BOOK. I’ve never been more emotionally unstable in my life. <br/><br/>Far from true, but still. I’m torn up inside.<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/01/12/the-world-gives-and-the-world-taketh-away-a-review-of-a-book-i-love-and-a-book-i-who-even-knows/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>I love the premise of it so much it hurts me to try to put it into words. But I will suffer through this pain for you.<br/><br/>So, <i>The School for Good and Evil</i> focuses on Sophie and Agatha. Sophie is beautiful, shallow, and a bit of a snob. Agatha is ugly, insecure, and very kind. They live in a world in which fairytales happen, and every yea</span>
  <span id="freeText5732139895144374740" style="display:none">AFGHASDFGASHDF THIS BOOK. I’ve never been more emotionally unstable in my life. <br /><br />Far from true, but still. I’m torn up inside.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/01/12/the-world-gives-and-the-world-taketh-away-a-review-of-a-book-i-love-and-a-book-i-who-even-knows/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br /><br />I love the premise of it so much it hurts me to try to put it into words. But I will suffer through this pain for you.<br /><br />So, <i>The School for Good and Evil</i> focuses on Sophie and Agatha. Sophie is beautiful, shallow, and a bit of a snob. Agatha is ugly, insecure, and very kind. They live in a world in which fairytales happen, and every year, the two kindest and most terrible children, respectively, from their village are kidnapped, never to return.<br /><br />But eventually, <i>they show up in the fairytales the children read.</i><br /><br />That’s actually one of about a thousand massive plot holes, but whatever. We’re not done yet, synopsis-wise.<br /><br />Sophie is obsessed with the idea of ending up in a fairytale. Agatha dreads the idea of becoming a witch.<br /><br />They’re both kidnapped, unsurprisingly. BUT PLOT TWIST: Agatha ends up in the School for Good, and Sophie, in the School for Evil.<br /><br />DUN DUN DUN.<br /><br />It’s actually a whole lot more boring than that. This book is a million pages long, and every possible bad side effect that could come with that does. It’s boring; it’s repetitive; it’s slow-moving; it’s filled with plot-holes; it’s supremely indecisive about its own themes, characters, and storylines.<br /><br />But.<br /><br /><i>That premise tho.</i><br /><br />I am so fully torn on EVERYTHING ELSE about this book. <br /><br />The characters: equal like and dislike. Agatha is pretty consistently adorable and likable; Sophie is occasionally a total badass, but most of the time so snobby and intolerable and mean. I just wanted her to accept her inner villain, and it was awesome when she did, BUT IT LASTED LIKE FIVE PAGES. Guh.<br /><br />The relationships: equal like and dislike. There’s this guy Tedros who is a total babe, and Sophie targets him, but I kinda like the him/Agatha schtick? Except it’s always made to be sooooo dramaaaaatic and just...yuck. There’s a big friendship with Sophie and Agatha, which I normally love (yay female friendship!) but it’s just so problematic sometimes. To quote the great Britney Spears: “toxic.”<br /><br />The themes: equal like and dislike. There’s a shaky theme of “no one is truly good or evil,” which is cool, except it completely ruins the chances of me seeing the badass villains I wanted so badly out of this book. It also seems like there’s some sort of attempt toward feminism, based off how short the princess end of the stick is compared to the princes’, but it never quite gets there???<br /><br />The premise versus the execution: Seriously one of the most brilliant, creative worlds I’ve EVER EVEN HEARD OF, but the execution can be just awful. SO MUCH WASTED POTENTIAL I COULD CRY.<br /><br />I don’t know. I guess I’ll read the sequel and see whether like or dislike wins out. (HA. Like whether “Good” or “Evil” wins in this book! I am so funny I impress even myself.)<br /><br />But then I’ll probably still read the third one either way, because I am both a massive pushover baby and a glutton for literary punishment.<br /><br />And I wonder why my average rating is so low.<br /><br />But I digress.<br /><br />Oh! I almost forgot! This absolutely, no way no how, is a children’s book. Nor is it YA. Nor should the characters be 12, or however old they are. That’s digusting.<br /><br />Yippee.<br /><br />Bottom line: I DON’T KNOW. WHO KNOWS. <br /><br />P.S.: The book trailer for this book is A M A Z I N G. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqnU3ZqvL1k&amp;feature=youtu.be">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqnU3...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5732139895144374740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2256295678" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2256295678" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2256295678?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062104892" href="/book/show/16248113-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2256295678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer857259812070800038"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517845421ra/25007317.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i> “She had always found villains more exciting than heroes. <br/>They had ambition, passion. <br/>They made the stories happen. <br/>Villains didn't fear death. <br/>No, they wrapped themselves in death like suits of armor!” </i> <br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>Did you ever wish you were part of a fairy tale like Snow White or Cinderella? <br/>Yes? Than that’s the perfect book for you. <br/>Every four years two children are kidnapped from Gavaldon and disappear. This year the mysterious man takes two girls, two friends: <br/>Sophie and Agatha. <br/>But wh</span>
  <span id="freeText857259812070800038" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517845421ra/25007317.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> “She had always found villains more exciting than heroes. <br>They had ambition, passion. <br>They made the stories happen. <br>Villains didn't fear death. <br>No, they wrapped themselves in death like suits of armor!” </i> <br><br>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Did you ever wish you were part of a fairy tale like Snow White or Cinderella? <br>Yes? Than that’s the perfect book for you. <br>Every four years two children are kidnapped from Gavaldon and disappear. This year the mysterious man takes two girls, two friends: <br>Sophie and Agatha. <br>But when they arrive a strange thing happens: the beautiful Sophie is send to the school of evil whereas Agatha is send to the school of good. The confused girls try to get into the right side of the schools and learn that nothing is as it seems. <br>Now an adventure begins in the school of fairytales, of good and evil. <br>First I was a little bit skeptical about the whole story, but the more I read, the more I loved the story. It was really really entertaining and the last 30% were filled with action, betrayal and really crazy stuff. <br>It was absolutely awesome! <br><br>Characters ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>I need to say I was a little bit skeptical with the characters. Even though they fitted the story, they felt a little bit... simple. <br>Their thoughts, dreams etc. <br>So so simple. <br>Go home/get to the right school/ save my friend/ get the prince<br>But the farther I got the more I learned to love the characters, especially Agatha. <br>But next to Agatha and Sophie the other characters felt really simple and plain. <br>Also I had a problem with the age of the characters, they didn’t feel like twelve year olds. The way they acted, the feelings they felt and other things made me always think that they were sixteen or at least fifteen. <br><br>World ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>There is a world where fairy tales exist. <br>And even though you wonder how can that be? That’s not the only thing. <br>The people in this stories - the princes, princesses, evil witches and monsters don’t appear from nowhere. <br>There are being taught at a school. <br>For every part of the fairy tale there is a school - one for good and one for evil. <br>And in there they learn how to fight, how to do magic, how to speak to animals and so on. <br>It’s really magical. <br>Absolutely perfect worldbuilding! <br><br>Relationships ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>The only real relationship I can see in this book is the one between Sophie and Agatha and - oh man! - is this a complicated one. <br>Even though I have no doubt at Agatha’s side of the friendship I was a little bit skeptical about Sophie. She’s really really egotistical and most thoughts in her mind are about herself (or her beauty/prince/hair). <br>But then.. they still had a really strong friendship and I really adored the way Agatha always thought about Sophie and her wellbeing and saving her and herself. <br>She always protected her friend and that was so so sweet. <br>I don’t want to say anything about the love story in this book, but it was not my favorite one, even though it was kind of sweet. <br><br>Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>I loved the story and the execution of it, but sometimes it still felt a little bit too simple for Young Adult and too much of a middle grade novel. But it was still really entertaining and I had fun reading it.<br>Maybe I’m just too critical, because I’m too old for this book. (Is 23 too old? Is it?🤷🏻‍♀️) <br>Either way I really liked this book and will continue with the rest of the series. 🎈</span>
  <a data-text-id="857259812070800038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1304413647&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1304413647" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14574077434420677997"><s>REVIEW TO COME TOMORROW</s><br/><br/>Second Read Review : <br/><br/><b>THE REVIEW IS POSTED </b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>"For he looked into your hearts and saw something very rare. Pure Good and Pure Evil."</b>
</i><br/><br/>this book was recommended to me by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4010776-makhda' rel='nofollow noopener'>my big sister</a>, she said that this book was good and she thought I would like it and I should tried reading it but that time I <b>hated</b> reading novels for no apparent reason. I just <b>hated</b> so I just ignored her recommendation until February 2015. I don't remember the exact date but I do remember that on February 2</span>
  <span id="freeText14574077434420677997" style="display:none"><s>REVIEW TO COME TOMORROW</s><br><br>Second Read Review : <br><br><b>THE REVIEW IS POSTED </b><br><br><i>
  <b>"For he looked into your hearts and saw something very rare. Pure Good and Pure Evil."</b>
</i><br><br>this book was recommended to me by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/4010776-makhda" rel="nofollow noopener">my big sister</a>, she said that this book was good and she thought I would like it and I should tried reading it but that time I <b>hated</b> reading novels for no apparent reason. I just <b>hated</b> so I just ignored her recommendation until February 2015. I don't remember the exact date but I do remember that on February 2015, I went into a bookstore just because I wanted to buy comics not a novel but I couldn't find any comics that I wanted to buy and then I saw this book and I remembered how my sister recommended it to me and she even said I would like it and I should tried reading it, So I decided to buy a copy and I <b>didn't</b> even think I would become a book lover, I just wanted to try it and if it's boring then I would stop reading it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443102209ra/16318739.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>but <b>my life has never been the same after I read this book. I have changed. </b> from being a person that hated novels to a person that can't live without novels because they help me to become a better person and they make me stronger to get through hard times. <b>I just can't live without books anymore.</b> so I wanted to say thank you very much to Mr. Chainani for writing this book because without this book, I wouldn't become this person and I wouldn't have all these amazing adventures that I got from novels. <b>this book changed my whole life and I never want to be the person I was before I became a book lover</b><br><br>now, lets talk about the book!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503169285ra/23635409.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I decided to reread this book because I used to love it and I gave it 5 stars so I wanted to know whether I still loved it or not and at first I didn't really enjoy it like it bored me but I kept reading it and the story got interesting and this book also made me laugh so much and I also found myself muttering like " JUST KISS! " way too many times and maybe that's because I mostly always read YA books <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420781351ra/13261471.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>and the pacing in this book was okay. it wasn't too fast or too slow. it was fine and when I reread it, I felt as if I was reading it for the first time because I didn't remember anything except the opening and the ending of this book but when I almost reached the ending, I somehow didn't feel as excited as I used to feel when I reached half of the book. I don't know why, though. *shrugs*<br><br>and this book has romance and in my opinion, the romance wasn't really good. it was kind of boring. I think I would enjoy it much more if it didn't have romance. <br><br>I honestly don't know why Agatha still wanted to be friends or best friend with Sophie, this girl hurt her! Agatha was so nice because if I were Agatha, I wouldn't want to be Sophie's friend anymore not after THIS!<br><br><b>
  <i> "Poor?" Agatha coughed. "You pushed me through a win-<br> dow!" </i>
</b><br><br>WHAT THE ACTUAL FUCK!? seriously, If I were Agatha I wouldn't care about Sophie anymore. Agatha's heart was so good, no wonder she got into School for Good. I tried the quiz and I was an Ever but still, if I were Agatha, maybe I would forgive Sophie but become her friend/best friend?? NO WAY. Sophie was crazy bitch. I mean didn't she think twice before she pushed Agatha? I know she was angry at Agatha but Agatha helped her several times! I could see how much Agatha love her and didn't she think about how much Agatha have helped her?! this girl is really an ungrateful bitch. <br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503178409ra/23636396.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>and few days ago while reading this book, I thought I would order the second and the third book but then after I finished reading it, I changed my mind. I won't order the sequels because I just don't really care about the ending or what will happen in the sequels and actually, this book was 3 stars for me but I gave one extra star because this book got me into reading and it also made me laugh and I don't laugh easily while reading. <br><br>thank you guys for reading and liking my review! hope you all have a nice day! <br><br>-------------------------------------------<br>First Read : 5 Stars <br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>GUYS! I tried the quiz and the result was I'm an Ever, I got accepted to the The School for Good ( with a soul score of 70% Good and 30% Evil ) But before taking the quiz, I thought I was a Never and I would get accepted to The School for Evil ... <br>what about you guys? Have you tried the quiz? If you have, which school you got accepted? What are you? A Never or an Ever? and what about your soul score? <br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><b>I AM REREADING IT!</b> <br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>THIS BOOK WAS THE BOOK THAT MADE ME LOVE READING BOOKS. I used to hate books without apparent reason and I'm STILL so grateful I tried reading this book because if I hadn't read this book, then I wouldn't have been here and I wouldn't have had all these awesome adventures with books.<br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~</span>
  <a data-text-id="14574077434420677997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_670904301" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/670904301" />
    <a title="Barb Middleton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4361541-barb-middleton"><img alt="Barb Middleton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329182394p2/4361541.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/670904301?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barb Middleton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barb Middleton" href="/user/show/4361541-barb-middleton">Barb Middleton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062104892" href="/book/show/16248113-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4361541-barb-middleton?shelf=fairy-tale">fairy-tale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4361541-barb-middleton?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer670904301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14568690165338109346">"Now I see why you two are friends," the prince says to the main characters Sophie and Agatha.<br/><br/>But... wait! I want to raise my hand and ask, "Tell me why they are friends!"<br/><br/>This is a problem considering the story hinges on this main point. While Sophie and Agatha are supposedly the best of friends, the character development doesn't show how this happens. When Agatha and Sophie first meet, Sophie isn't Agatha's friend and she says so; she realizes Sophie's just using her. Sophie is beautiful, shall</span>
  <span id="freeText14568690165338109346" style="display:none">"Now I see why you two are friends," the prince says to the main characters Sophie and Agatha.<br /><br />But... wait! I want to raise my hand and ask, "Tell me why they are friends!"<br /><br />This is a problem considering the story hinges on this main point. While Sophie and Agatha are supposedly the best of friends, the character development doesn't show how this happens. When Agatha and Sophie first meet, Sophie isn't Agatha's friend and she says so; she realizes Sophie's just using her. Sophie is beautiful, shallow, and narcissistic. Sophie wants to go the School of Good and Evil where two children are kidnapped every year from her village later to be found in a fairy tale storybook. She believes she will find her prince at the School of Good and live "happily ever after." Agatha is the perfect villain for the School of Evil, Sophie thinks, because she is ugly, lonely, and isolated, and Sophie thinks if she's with Agatha her chance of being chosen will be more likely. When Sophie is kidnapped (just as she wants) Agatha tries to rescue her and in the process the two end up at the school except Sophie doesn't go to the School of Good, she ends up in the School of Evil, while Agatha is dumped in the School of Good.<br /><br />The two misfits continue to be friends but mainly because Agatha pursues it the most. She goes to extremes to rescue Sophie and it never made sense to me given Sophie's quickness to betray Agatha at every turn and Agatha's dislike for her at the beginning. Sophie and Agatha are superficial and flit between wanting beauty on the outside to beauty on the inside. Agatha says in the beginning that beauty is temporary but later confesses she thinks it brings happiness. Sophie believes only in beauty with no understanding of ugliness that comes from hate. Her personality struck me as psychopathic, probably because she resembled the murders I just read about in a nonfiction book called, "Greed, Rage, and Love Gone Wrong: Murder in Minnesota," by Bruce Rubenstein. She cheats, murders, and lies with no remorse and Agatha goes along with her because she is her only friend. Sophie's dumber than a doorknob most of the time before transforming into a mastermind villain at the end. An explanation for her surge of brainpower is given, but it felt contrived. The characters are stereotypical and wishy-washy for a good portion of the novel. They start to come together at the end but I wasn't vested in their development because it took too long.<br /><br />The bag of mixed messages continues with the prince, Tedros, who loves one and then the other meanwhile badmouthing each when dating the other girl. He seemed pretty hypocritical to me when he says to Sophie she's a terrible friend because she uses her friends, betrays them, calls them fat, and liars. He too, is prejudiced toward others, lies, and betrays people who are different. The seesaw continues as Agatha hounds Sophie to impulsively kiss Tedros immediately and then lectures her later for not making a plan of attack to kiss him. Teachers are like caricatures that don't offer words of advice. For instance, when Agatha and Sophie are punished by the teachers in burning shoes until the girls want to die, I thought it focused on the cruelty of the teachers versus the girls argument. The teachers are mostly idiots throughout the story with no control of students. When some teachers impart a few words of wisdom at the end, it seemed out of character and too late. I also didn't like the message that failure is unacceptable and students who failed were dealt an awful fate. Failure is difficult to deal with and those who failed were the kids the author kills off the most. <br /><br />The ending and what it suggests might offend some. I won't give it away but I didn't see that coming. It is one of many reasons it is better for older students. Some of the plot is predictable such as the love triangle, but there were also some interesting twists such as when Sophie has to deal with a duplicate of herself in class creating an introspective moment. Unfortunately there were too few of these occurrences which makes the book fall short of its potential. Transitions were confusing at times such as when Sophie and Agatha would talk to each other in mirrors. I seemed to always be rereading those parts because I didn't' realize they were looking at their reflection to see the other. The action scenes and magic is very creative and I enjoyed these parts. <br /><br />There is a reader prophecy and riddle. The prophecy didn't seem necessary to the plot because it wasn't told until the end. The overarching theme of good and evil in human nature fell flat because the characters weren't complex enough. The stereotypes enforced in this book are my biggest complaint. That ugly people aren't happy unless they are beautiful, that a girl isn't happy unless she has her prince, that girls only think of boys, that a fat person has no friends, that a married person isn't happy. Some of these are refuted at the end but it comes too late. Or perhaps the author is trying to do too much. At one point Sophie tries to rally the villains into having hope and feeling good about themselves. At first her advice surrounds just superficial beauty before turning toward what it means to accept oneself, but the message never gets delved into because the plot suddenly shifts into a Dark Lord hullabaloo; thus, losing the opportunity to dig deeper into this theme. This book's potential isn't reached and it is a shame because it is an interesting premise and creative fantasy. Maybe the sequel will pull it all together.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14568690165338109346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_560405516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/560405516" />
    <a title="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews"><img alt="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603380977p2/4863162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/560405516?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" href="/user/show/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews">Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062104892" href="/book/show/16248113-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=faint-praise-award">faint-praise-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=tales-of-fae-and-faery-tales">tales-of-fae-and-faery-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=edelweiss-arc">edelweiss-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=reviews-2013">reviews-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer560405516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18316785304597501185"><b>Read <a href='http://agelesspagesreviews.blogspot.com/2013/05/blog-post.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Review</a> & More Like It <a href='http://agelesspagesreviews.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>On My Blog</a>!</b><br/><br/><br/>First of all, if <a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqnU3ZqvL1k' rel='nofollow noopener'>the awesome book trailer for <i>The School of Good and Evil</i></a> is what created an interest in Chainani's fiction debut, all I can tell you is this:<br/><br/> <a href='http://s1331.photobucket.com/user/jeskimokimono/media/how-to-stop-being-single_zpse11a9769.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413284ra/813519.gif' alt=' photo how-to-stop-being-single_zpse11a9769.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>(Even watching that trailer now, after the fact, I am excited and impressed. And then I remember. And then woe.)<br/><br/>The book sadly doesn't live up to the awesomeness that advertised it. I'm not even a fan of book trailers, but the promotion department for this book deserves a big raise. The editin</span>
  <span id="freeText18316785304597501185" style="display:none"><b>Read <a href="http://agelesspagesreviews.blogspot.com/2013/05/blog-post.html" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review</a> &amp; More Like It <a href="http://agelesspagesreviews.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">On My Blog</a>!</b><br><br><br>First of all, if <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqnU3ZqvL1k" rel="nofollow noopener">the awesome book trailer for <i>The School of Good and Evil</i></a> is what created an interest in Chainani's fiction debut, all I can tell you is this:<br><br> <a href="http://s1331.photobucket.com/user/jeskimokimono/media/how-to-stop-being-single_zpse11a9769.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380413284ra/813519.gif" alt=" photo how-to-stop-being-single_zpse11a9769.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>(Even watching that trailer now, after the fact, I am excited and impressed. And then I remember. And then woe.)<br><br>The book sadly doesn't live up to the awesomeness that advertised it. I'm not even a fan of book trailers, but the promotion department for this book deserves a big raise. The editing department might not. But, if you're just now hearing about this YA/MG fantasy about fairytales and witches and princesses, this might end up being the book for you. It's a tad long, a tad overwrought, but it's got a lot of heart and, at times, can be very entertaining. Soman Chainani creates a vibrant world with two interesting and diverse leads, and I can say they paths and plots he takes them through isn't predictable, though it can be a tad pedantic at times. The comparisons to Gregpry Maguire's work is apt and appropriate and I can see his fans enjoying this less adult look at magical children.<br><br><i>The School for Good and Evil</i> reminded me of a younger Harry Potter at times. There's the obvious: magical children spirited away for their edification (for either good or ill), there's the obvious good guys, the obvious bad guys, magical beings like werewolves, fairies, and a multi-headed dog inside a mysterious, hidden castle(s). There are pranks, a ball, a love story that is not what you expect, and in the end, a grand battle for the school itself. That all sounds well and good and like fun, and it can be. The main problem is that <i>The School for Good and Evil</i> takes too long to get anywhere. It becomes too predictable to shock readers and the final conflict... well, veered on deus ex machina. That's never a good way to resolve a story readers have spent so much time investing in.<br><br>This is a looooong book for almost any genre (I'm looking at you, Epic Fantasy), but for a very young YA/verging on MG fairytale, 496 pages is just much too much. The pacing lags, events feel drawn out or stretched beyond feasibility, and the plot takes too much time to really form. There's a lack of tension and suspense before key events because the author takes too long to develop any sort of meaningful conflict. Outside of plotting and pacing, Chainani is an obviously talented, very visual, writer. Scenes pop and creatures both big and small, humor or non, all burst from the page. <i>The School for Good and Evil</i> can project an image, but fails to deliver real substance to go with how pretty/evil everything is on the surface.<br> <br>The main characters are adaptable, and pretty well-rounded. There's more to both Sophie and Agatha than what meets the eye, and the author's switcheroo can be pretty clever. However, like most things in this novel, the realizations that come to both girls about their roles in future fairy tales takes far too long to foment into something meaningful. I could have done without the romances that pop up and complicate the girls' relationship and the plot, but Prince Charmings (and Not So Charmings) are to be expected in a novel so concerned with fairytales. The characters are another strong aspect of the novel, and I'm curious to see what will happen after the final events of book one.<br><br><i>The School for Good and Evil</i> isn't a bad book by any means. It's just not as good as you, or I, or that book trailer want it to be. Those looking for a saccharine-ly sweet Disney tale should look elsewhere, and readers in search of a vibrant setting with complex and contradictory characters will find <i>The School for Good and Evil</i> a good fit, if not a particularly memorable one. There's some room for improvement, and editing, but Soman Chainani has a satisfactory beginning to his new series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18316785304597501185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_627456842" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/627456842" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14811808-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585394064p2/14811808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/627456842?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/14811808-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062104892" href="/book/show/16248113-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=children-s-lit-and-middle-grade">children-s-lit-and-middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer627456842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14452829169160540832"><i>So, again, I had a feeling about this book. Before even starting it I knew I'd like it, probably even love it. And it proved me right.</i><br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392810092i/8614989.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"Agatha, you dressed as a <i>bride</i> for Halloween."<br/>"Weddings are scary."</b>
</blockquote><br/>It's impossible for me to dislike a character after such a statement. From the very first page I was sucked into the magical realm of the School for Good and Evil and it didn't let me go until the very last word. <br/><br/>Sophie is a princess at heart. She loves pink, is beautiful, cares for her lo</span>
  <span id="freeText14452829169160540832" style="display:none"><i>So, again, I had a feeling about this book. Before even starting it I knew I'd like it, probably even love it. And it proved me right.</i><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392810092i/8614989.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Agatha, you dressed as a <i>bride</i> for Halloween."<br>"Weddings are scary."</b>
</blockquote><br>It's impossible for me to dislike a character after such a statement. From the very first page I was sucked into the magical realm of the School for Good and Evil and it didn't let me go until the very last word. <br><br>Sophie is a princess at heart. She loves pink, is beautiful, cares for her looks and Good Deeds and wants nothing more but to be kidnapped and brought to the School. <br>Agatha is the proclaimed witch. The villagers avoid her, she lives on a graveyard with her mother and her black cat Reaper, avoids mirrors, wears black and is all grumpy and dark. <br>But when both girls are kidnapped, everything turns out entirely different since Sophie is dropped into the School for Evil and Agatha into the one for Good. <br>A terrible mistake. <br>But soon the question arises whether it is really a mistake or maybe they are exactly where they belong? <br><br>Sophie acts the way I always imagined a true princess act- spoiled and self-absorbed. She cares for nothing but <i>her</i> looks, <i>her</i> reputation and <i>herself</i>. Whenever she tries to be good it turns out twisted and wrong, whenever she fights, she does for the wrong reasons. <br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392810092i/8614990.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote> <br>Under all the pink layers hides something unexpected and dangerous. Of course she has quite a rough background, but it doesn't redeem her. <br>I cannot say I hated or even disliked Sophie, because I didn't. At first I thought everyone in this book would be just a simple, sweet fairy-tale character, but the book soon proved me wrong. <br>The struggles, doubts, fears and conflicts went much deeper then in a childish, simple fairy-tale. In a way, many dark parts of the book addressed the real-world and showed that the same darkness is as present in our life as in a fairy-tale. <br><br>Agatha on the other hand, with all her cynical attitude and dark clothes and, well, 'ugliness' is anything but evil. She is <u>good</u>, but not the fairy-tale, glittery kind of good. She is <b>
  <i>real</i>
</b>. She makes mistakes, misunderstands, tries to help her friend, knows compassion as well as antipathy and has lots and lots of fears and doubts. <br>Not only was she a conflicted and confused character at first, oh no, she was the embodiment of so many young people of the nowadays world. Although she, just like Sophie, messed up, I found myself grinning instead of complaining. Maybe because I knew I'd have made the same mistakes, who knows. <br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392810606i/8615189._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>I loved Dot and Hester just as much as I loved Agatha and Sophie. I liked Tedros, the prince, who was also far less fairy-talish (is it even a word? I guess it isn't.) than I expected him to be and even the School Master. <br>Their actions made sense and what was even more important, they made them come alive. <br>And the ending. Oh my, the ending was <b>
  <i>brilliant!</i>
</b> This book generally was <b>
  <i>unpredictable</i>
</b>, but the ending itself was like being hit with a book in the face. <br><br>I loved the plot progression, the character development, simply everything! It wasn't perfect, but it was <b>
  <i>real, beautiful, enchanting</i>
</b>. <br>The questions that were asked in this book addressed our world as much as the magical one and the given answers were just as important. <br>Many of the contemporary books that mean to be realistic and address real-life problems and conflicts aren't as true-to-life as this fantasy, fairy-tale book. <br>They often feel plain and boring repeating words that have been said already and describing what has been discussed long ago and providing ideas and answers and solutions through <i>saying</i> instead of <i>showing</i>. <br>This book <i>showed</i> solutions and ideas. <br><br>Not only was it beautiful and full of light and hope, but it provided so many useful arguments and showed many of the now existing problems. It was impossible for me to not-love this book and I <u>highly recommend</u> it not only to those who love fairy-tales, but to everyone in need of reading something beautiful and hopeful!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14452829169160540832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062104892" href="/book/show/16248113-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=library">library</a>,

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18351540399351057718">Impressive world-building, bogged down by so. much. plot. <br/><br/>They tried to escape umpteen times. The Good and Evil sides faced off another umpteen times (but someone would always back down). The ending went on and on, with magical and physical battles as well as riddle and prophecy solving. It needed an editor to rein it in very badly. Many of the minor characters were interchangeable, as were the teachers. I had trouble remembering which of the teachers taught at which school, since they all mingl</span>
  <span id="freeText18351540399351057718" style="display:none">Impressive world-building, bogged down by so. much. plot. <br /><br />They tried to escape umpteen times. The Good and Evil sides faced off another umpteen times (but someone would always back down). The ending went on and on, with magical and physical battles as well as riddle and prophecy solving. It needed an editor to rein it in very badly. Many of the minor characters were interchangeable, as were the teachers. I had trouble remembering which of the teachers taught at which school, since they all mingled so freely, and since the girls were perpetually running back and forth, interacting with people from both sides. <br /><br />But the idea is so very creative, and I really loved Agatha and even Sophie, though at times she was too over-the-top. The descriptions of clothing, of the castles and dungeons and classrooms made of candy, were so great. I really liked the way it played with the concept of good and evil, of how our intentions can lead us astray. <br /><br />Seriously though, this book could have been a tight 300 pages and not lost a thing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18351540399351057718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_891437087" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/891437087" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/891437087?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062104892" href="/book/show/16248113-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=cotton-candy">cotton-candy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=witches-warlocks-and-magic">witches-warlocks-and-magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer891437087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17320934604353160042"><b>Kindle deal for a limited time 02May18 <a href='https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B009NF6FYI/ref=s9_acsd_hps_bw_c_KCKDDGBs_3_w?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-3&pf_rd_r=25YFMCCF21WHKFZY3YRR&pf_rd_r=25YFMCCF21WHKFZY3YRR&pf_rd_t=101&pf_rd_p=812491f2-d136-45f8-adfa-a27a98647709&pf_rd_p=812491f2-d136-45f8-adfa-a27a98647709&pf_rd_i=11552285011' rel='nofollow noopener'>$1.99 on Amazon</a></b><br/><br/><b>Once upon a time a girl dreamt of being kidnapped….</b><br/><br/>Wait..What? <br/><br/>Every four years two children from the village are taken away, whisked off to a school where they learn how to be in a fairy tale. One of the children could end up a hero while the other is destined to be the villain. Sophie is sure that once she is taken she will get to find her prince and her happily ever after. She has even found the girl from the village who she is sure will b</span>
  <span id="freeText17320934604353160042" style="display:none"><b>Kindle deal for a limited time 02May18 <a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B009NF6FYI/ref=s9_acsd_hps_bw_c_KCKDDGBs_3_w?pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&amp;pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-3&amp;pf_rd_r=25YFMCCF21WHKFZY3YRR&amp;pf_rd_r=25YFMCCF21WHKFZY3YRR&amp;pf_rd_t=101&amp;pf_rd_p=812491f2-d136-45f8-adfa-a27a98647709&amp;pf_rd_p=812491f2-d136-45f8-adfa-a27a98647709&amp;pf_rd_i=11552285011" rel="nofollow noopener">$1.99 on Amazon</a></b><br /><br /><b>Once upon a time a girl dreamt of being kidnapped….</b><br /><br />Wait..What? <br /><br />Every four years two children from the village are taken away, whisked off to a school where they learn how to be in a fairy tale. One of the children could end up a hero while the other is destined to be the villain. Sophie is sure that once she is taken she will get to find her prince and her happily ever after. She has even found the girl from the village who she is sure will be her counterpart and befriended her…that’s how good she is. Agatha is sure that Sophie is crazy and there is no such place, let alone why does she have to be the villain.<br />On the outside it makes perfect sense. Sophie is beautiful, blonde, wears pink dresses and can sing while Agatha has straggly black hair, carries dead things in her pockets and lives in a graveyard.<br /> <br /><i>“Say I sink to your intelligence level and pretend to believe all this. Why am I going to villain school? Why has everyone elected me the mistress of evil?”<br />“No one says you’re evil Agatha,” Sophie sighed. “You’re just different.”<br />Agatha narrowed her eyes, “Different how?.....”<br /> “….For the Create a Tale competition your story ended with Snow White eaten by vultures and Cinderella drowning in a tub.”<br />“I thought it was a better ending.”<br />“You gave me a dead frog for my birthday.”<br />“To remind you we all die and end up rotting underground eaten by maggots, so we should enjoy our birthdays while we have them. I found it thoughtful.”</i><br /><br />Agatha has never had a friend before Sophie so when a shadow comes to steal her in the middle of the night Agatha tries desperately to save her friend. They are both taken but everything seems to go wrong when Sophie is dropped into the grounds of the School for Evil and Agatha is sent to the school for good. It must be a mistake Sophie is sure she is good, she must meet her Prince, fall in love and get her Happily Ever After. Agatha doesn’t want to be at the school, the only thing she cares about is saving Sophie and getting home. <br /><br />It is all harder than it seems and to survive each must do well in the school they’ve been assigned to or suffer a fate worse than death.<br /><br />In the School for good, Agatha can’t help but notice that the Good might all be beautiful and princesses and sure they are supposed to be courageous and kind but mostly they seem vapid and selfish. All the princesses want is a prince to love. Their biggest goal is to get a prince to ask them to the ball or suffer a fate worse than death. As far as Agatha is concerned<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“love is something storybooks invented to keep girls busy”</i>
</b><br /><br />In the School for Evil, Sophie is at a loss for why she would have ever been placed there. She is a princess, just look at her. There has been a terrible mistake but she is convinced if she can just get a prince to kiss her everything will be fine.<br /><br />I had such a fun time reading this. It makes fun of itself. Agatha was incredibly likeable from the beginning and Sophie grows on you but it takes a lot of time. Sophie is harder to love because she is probably 75% evil and 25% good. Sometimes she goes a little overboard. I loved the friendship between the two girls and how much Agatha really cared for Sophie and just wanted to go back to the village so they could still be friends.<br /><br />The side characters of the evil school were also a lot of fun, as evil characters are. They are just misunderstood by the other side. They are the children of famous fairy tale villains and sure they’ve had stirring of love before but luckily they’ve been stamped out by their families early.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“First time I told my dad I liked a girl, he slathered me in honey and sealed me in a bear den for a night. Haven’t liked one since.”<br /> “First time I told my mother I fancied someone, she baked me in an oven for an hour,” Mona agreed, green skin paling. “I never think about boys now.”<br /> “First time I liked a boy, my dad killed him.”</i>
</b><br /><br />And of course there is a Prince. Tedros is everything Sophie is sure she wants and deserves. Son to King Arthur he is the most desirable of all the princes. <br /><br /><i>He glistened with a noble sheen as if his blood ran purer than the rest. The stranger took one look at the frowning sword armed boys pulled his own sword and grinned.<br />Forty boys came at him at once but he disarmed each with lightning speed the swords of his classmates piled up beneath his feet as he flicked them away without inflicting a scratch.<br />Sophie gaped bewitched<br />Agatha hoped he’d impale himself. But no such luck.</i><br /><br />There were some great classes and challenges that were a good time to read through and I loved the push pull of the friendship between Sophie and Agatha. The ending was a little different than I expected but I really enjoyed the twist at the end. I liked so many of the ideas behind this story and it will be interesting to see where the author took it in the next book which I will of course be reading soon.<br /><br />Recommended for when you want something fun that is more about friendships than romances. Great MG reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17320934604353160042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_946584742" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/946584742" />
    <a title="Inge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6278820-inge"><img alt="Inge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556214992p2/6278820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/946584742?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inge" href="/user/show/6278820-inge">Inge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780007492947" href="/book/show/18778100-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=faeries-fae-elves">faeries-fae-elves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=feelgood-wholesome">feelgood-wholesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=villain-antihero-love">villain-antihero-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer946584742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14625911262301421852"><i>"Who needs princes in our fairy tale?"</i><br/><br/>I'm going to kick my past self for never picking up this book when I've wanted to read it for so long. Look at all the fun I missed out on! This was SO good.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_675738731" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/675738731" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10095657-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341435512p2/10095657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/675738731?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/10095657-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062104892" href="/book/show/16248113-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer675738731&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer675738731" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4058484803657351255">****MASSIVE SPOILER ALERT****<br/>***okay don't say I didn't warn you***<br/><br/>The School for Good and Evil has a great premise: Sophie desperately wants to get out of the tiny village where she lives. Every four years two children are kidnapped from this village, one Good and one Evil, to go to the School for Good and Evil that prepares them to take their part in fairy tales. Sophie wants to be a princess, and win her prince. While everyone else in the village hides and uglifies their (good) children when </span>
  <span id="freeText4058484803657351255" style="display:none">****MASSIVE SPOILER ALERT****<br />***okay don't say I didn't warn you***<br /><br />The School for Good and Evil has a great premise: Sophie desperately wants to get out of the tiny village where she lives. Every four years two children are kidnapped from this village, one Good and one Evil, to go to the School for Good and Evil that prepares them to take their part in fairy tales. Sophie wants to be a princess, and win her prince. While everyone else in the village hides and uglifies their (good) children when the School Master comes a-kidnapping, Sophie plans to entice him to take her.<br /><br />One of Sophie's conscious good deeds is to befriend the ugly and unwanted girl who lives in the cemetary. Agatha only has one friend, one person who values her. When Sophie attempts to get kidnapped, Agatha tries to save her, and they both end up taken by the School Master. But then Sophie ends up in the School for Evil, and Agatha ends up in the School for Good. Both believe they are in the wrong place.<br /><br />All this by pg 41. So far, excellent! What a great idea! And this is why I gave the book 2 stars. And then we have 447 more pages of what happens when they get to the school. <br /><br />Agatha wants to go home. Sophie wants to change schools. And she wants to win a prince of her own (you have to get one to ask you to the Ball. Only the Goods have a ball.) All the Good children are beautiful. Agatha is not, so she doesn't feel she belongs. All the Evil children are ugly, some to the point of serious deformation. Sophie is beautiful, so no one feels she belongs. She is told there are never any mistakes.<br /><br />So, we're going to find in the end that Agatha is really good, and Sophie was only faking being good so she's actually Evil. But that doesn't make sense, because Sophie may not be that good, but that doesn't make her evil. But this would make some kind of sense. What actually happens, doesn't.<br /><br />The equivalence of goodness and beauty is revolting. The objective for the girls, to get the prince of their choice to ask them to the Ball, where they may receive their kiss, is likewise revolting. <br /><br />The adventures that Agatha and Sophie undergo are so over the top, they are hard to follow. But no matter what happens to them, from almost drowning, to being taken to the torture chamber and murdering the torturer, there are never any emotional or physical consequences.<br /><br />Sophie has roommates in her Evil tower room; Agatha has classmates in the Good school, but after 400 pages, there were so undifferentiated, I was still having trouble remembering who was who, with only a very few exceptions. The same went for the teachers. Description doesn't go nearly as far to make a character memorable as behavior. Dot, Hort, Beatrix and Tedros can be told apart. The rest all run together. <br /><br />If a climactic event happens in a story, and in the next line you have to explain what just happened, and why it is important, that is a strong sign that you need to go back to an earlier place (or two) in your story and set it up. When the event occurs, the audience should enjoy it will full understanding as it happens. <br /><br />Agatha is the main character, and yet the final move is given to Sophie. Agatha becoming the most beautiful princess ever, was really revolting. Really? Beauty and goodness are the same thing? And she always was that beautiful and didn't know it? That's just not true. And if there's one thing fiction should never do, it's tell lies. This may sound like a paradox, but the purpose of fiction is to create situations that reveal truths about humanity. If stories say things about people that are not true, then they have no purpose.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4058484803657351255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4042021677062706446">[4 Stars] Well that was a whirlwind of an adventure if I ever read one! It was fun, hilarious at times, gruesome and shocking, and also just action packed and heart wrenching. I'm still trying to figure out what exactly Chainani is trying to say in this. But there are certain things that happen in this story that slightly bewilder me. I did enjoy the </span>
  <span id="freeText4042021677062706446" style="display:none">[4 Stars] Well that was a whirlwind of an adventure if I ever read one! It was fun, hilarious at times, gruesome and shocking, and also just action packed and heart wrenching. I'm still trying to figure out what exactly Chainani is trying to say in this. I get that the main message is that good and evil are more shades of grey than anything else, and it also emphasizes the importance of friendship. But there are certain things that happen in this story that slightly bewilder me. I did enjoy the setting, characters, and writing though and am looking forward to diving into the next one. I think Chainani's master plan for the characters and their development will probably become clearer as I read on!</span>

<div id="review_633921716" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/633921716" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/633921716?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062104892" href="/book/show/16248113-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=signed">signed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer633921716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12186318378691274774">Adorable and adventurous, The School for Good and Evil is a fun escape from reality. When beautiful Sophie and weird Agatha end up in the wrong school - perfect Sophie can't be evil now, can she? - they're determined to fix this unforgiving mistake. <br/><br/>This is a magical adventure through and through; the book is set at this School of Good and Evil, a wonderfully imaginative school that trains future fairy tale characters. Meaning when you graduate, you'll be in a fairy tale book; whether a princess</span>
  <span id="freeText12186318378691274774" style="display:none">Adorable and adventurous, The School for Good and Evil is a fun escape from reality. When beautiful Sophie and weird Agatha end up in the wrong school - perfect Sophie can't be evil now, can she? - they're determined to fix this unforgiving mistake. <br><br>This is a magical adventure through and through; the book is set at this School of Good and Evil, a wonderfully imaginative school that trains future fairy tale characters. Meaning when you graduate, you'll be in a fairy tale book; whether a princess, a villain, a gremlin, or even a tree, your faith will be determined by how well you do at this school. This idea kind of blew my mind a little; I found it so unique and incredibly fun. The girls, each clearly thinking they're in the wrong school, are determined to trade places, but this proves to be quite the challenge. Told in a dual POV, we have Sophie who's the picture perfect of a true princess fighting against face warts and drab clothes; while her strange, ugly friend (her words!) is stuck being taught how to be a perfect princess in a perfect pink dress that was clearly meant for Sophie. This role reversal is both amusing and kind of refreshing. It shows that what's on the outside doesn't always reflect the person's true self, sending an important message to young'uns. Sophie is an obvious brat who thinks a good deed involves teaching others how not to be ugly anymore. It makes you happy that she's finally learning a lesson on what being good really means. These two protagonists are polar opposites, both offering the book their own dash of charm and warmth. <br><br>The great characterization doesn't stop at these two, we have a vast number of characters by their side who fill up the book with humor, mischief, magic, and lively personalities. These include teachers and students, as well as various magical beings ranging from gargoyles to wish fish. If this isn't enough to charm you (be difficult, why don't you) check out the delightful illustrations we're treated to at every chapter beginning:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380424279i/845752._SY540_.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Furthermore, the plot has an intriguing mystery element involving the school master and its history which had me entranced. I loved the idea of the battle that turned the master into a mystery himself, leaving me dying to know more. Moreover, <i>everything</i> surrounding this whole story is mysteriously compelling. It's also highly creative with magical touches at every corner - an MG novel perfect for fans of Harry Potter and the likes. As the plot can become a bit dark, even sinister at times, I would hesitate to recommend it to the younger end of MG readers, but I recommend it to everyone else - young and old. You'll never find yourself bored, and you're bound to feel the book's enchanting atmosphere the minute you open its cover, just look at it:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380424279i/845753.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>--<br><i>A copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236618i/681468.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_1860398775" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1860398775" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56662187-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539790744p2/56662187.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1860398775?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/56662187-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062104892" href="/book/show/16248113-the-school-for-good-and-evil">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1860398775" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14593733675953139500">I was searching for a middle grade book with complicated characters and interesting themes; that is exactly what I found in The School for Good and Evil. Friendship is one of the things this book focusses on most. Agatha and Sophie look like a pair that no one would expect, but their bond continually survives all the obstacles thrown at them. Ultimately it is what's most important in their lives.<br/><br/>My favorite part of this book was the question posed again and again. What is it to be good? Is it ab</span>
  <span id="freeText14593733675953139500" style="display:none">I was searching for a middle grade book with complicated characters and interesting themes; that is exactly what I found in The School for Good and Evil. Friendship is one of the things this book focusses on most. Agatha and Sophie look like a pair that no one would expect, but their bond continually survives all the obstacles thrown at them. Ultimately it is what's most important in their lives.<br /><br />My favorite part of this book was the question posed again and again. What is it to be good? Is it about looking good, looking like you are loving? Or is it about being selfless and viewing the world as what is true instead of the exterior? Agatha was my favorite character because she viewed the world in the latter way. She forgave Sophie again and again, holding out hope that she would change. Agatha also understood (or came to understand) that the world is not black and white, good and evil. It is full of humans who are both together. <br /><br />I also enjoyed the atmospheric writing style. At times, it was difficult to understand because I was trying to grasp every single detail. That's not how this book is meant to be read. It's written not to give you a play by play, especially in the action scenes, but to convey magic and a picture. It's very whimsical. The author captured the feeling of the original Grimm Fairytales in this book. <br /><br />Overall I enjoyed it a lot. I didn't give it five stars because the first half of the book was a bit slow for me, but halfway through it picked up, and I said outloud, "this is great." I can't wait to continue the trilogy and see where these characters go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14593733675953139500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12418197542603394835">This book was great, this book takes a unique spin on classic fairy tales and how their viewed. This is shown well with the two main characters Sophie and Agatha, based on what a classic princess and villain should look like dictates that Sophie "the princess" and Agatha "the villain" but toys with expectations based on appearance. Something that I really liked about this book is the strong friendship between the two main female characters, also the power of forgiving others even when they don't</span>
  <span id="freeText12418197542603394835" style="display:none">This book was great, this book takes a unique spin on classic fairy tales and how their viewed. This is shown well with the two main characters Sophie and Agatha, based on what a classic princess and villain should look like dictates that Sophie "the princess" and Agatha "the villain" but toys with expectations based on appearance. Something that I really liked about this book is the strong friendship between the two main female characters, also the power of forgiving others even when they don't necessary deserve it. The ending was fantastic and I cannot wait to continue the series to see where things go next.</span>
